    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

        state: 'apple_oauth_state_1aa3ae3f-bfa3-4c58-8da6-2fa9dffdd677'

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer1855681151546285927">Before he had a family, before he met Moominmamma, Moominpappa led a life of adventure and intrigue. But he's never told his story until now.<br/>Now Moominpappa has a bad cold, and it's the perfect time to remember his youthful endeavors and to ponder the Experiences which have made him the remarkable Moomin he is. As he reads each chapter aloud to Moomintroll, Snufkin, and Sn</span>
  <span id="freeText1855681151546285927" style="display:none">Before he had a family, before he met Moominmamma, Moominpappa led a life of adventure and intrigue. But he's never told his story until now.<br />Now Moominpappa has a bad cold, and it's the perfect time to remember his youthful endeavors and to ponder the Experiences which have made him the remarkable Moomin he is. As he reads each chapter aloud to Moomintroll, Snufkin, and Sniff, they, and we, learn of his triumphs and tribulations, and his momentous meetings with the Joxter, the Muddler, and a cast of other characters too incredible (especially Edward the Booble) to list here.<br />"Moominpappa's Memoirs" has never before been translated into English, and Farrar, Straus and Giroux is proud to be able to add this title to its other Moomin books.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1855681151546285927" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>
</div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2249228652" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6607323860351170289"><a href='https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=KlYG1hggK8c' rel='nofollow noopener'>Click here</a> to watch a video review of this book on my channel, <i>From Beginning to Bookend</i>.<br/><br/><a href='https://imgur.com/JOQrpqU' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1517418713i/24975476._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>Jansson's decision to switch to a first-person perspective enlivens this darling account of young Moominpappa navigating one quirky adventure after another. <br/><br/></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1877267687" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer13105345620025199449">I must be terribly unobservant; despite having read the Mumintroll series on and off for several decades, I had somehow not noticed that Snusmumriken and his father Joxaren are Zen masters. But this passage was so obvious that even I couldn't miss it:<blockquote><i>När Fredrikson avlöste mig vid rodret i gryningen nämnde jag i förbigående Joxarens förvånande och fullkomliga brist på intresse för omgivningen.<br/><br/>Hm, sa Fredrikson. Kanske han tvärtom bryr sig om allting? Vi bryr oss om en enda sak. Du vill bli. Jag </i></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText13105345620025199449" style="display:none">I must be terribly unobservant; despite having read the Mumintroll series on and off for several decades, I had somehow not noticed that Snusmumriken and his father Joxaren are Zen masters. But this passage was so obvious that even I couldn't miss it:<blockquote><i>När Fredrikson avlöste mig vid rodret i gryningen nämnde jag i förbigående Joxarens förvånande och fullkomliga brist på intresse för omgivningen.<br /><br />Hm, sa Fredrikson. Kanske han tvärtom bryr sig om allting? Vi bryr oss om en enda sak. Du vill bli. Jag vill göra. Mitt brorsbarn vill ha. Men Joxaren bara lever.<br /><br />Äsch, leva! Det kan ju vem som helst, sa jag.<br /><br />Hm, sade Fredrikson.<br /><br />Hur som helst, Joxarens inställning förefaller mig på något sätt slarvigt, jag menar det där att bara leva. Leva gör man väl i alla fall? Som jag ser saken är man hela tiden omgiven av massor med viktiga och betydelsefulla saker som borde upplevas och tänkas ut och erövras, det finns så fullt av möjligheter att nackhåret reser sig på ända när jag tänker på dem - och i mitten sitter jag själv och är naturligtvis det allra viktigast.</i><br /><br />(My translation)<br /><br />When Fredrikson relieved me at the tiller towards dawn, I mentioned in passing Joxaren's inexplicable and total lack of interest in what went on around him.<br /><br />Hm, said Fredrikson. Maybe, on the contrary, he cares about everything? We only care about one thing. You want to become something. I want to do something. My nephew wants to own something. But Joxaren just exists.<br /><br />Fiddle-de-dee, exist! I said. Anyone can do that.<br /><br />Hm, said Fredrikson.<br /><br />At any rate, Joxaren's attitude seems somehow irresponsible to me, I mean this business of just existing. We all exist anyway, don't we? The way I see it, you're constantly surrounded by any number of important and meaningful things that need to be experienced and thought about and conquered, there are so many possibilities that the hair on the back of my head stands on end when I just think about them - and in the middle, here I am, needless to say the most important thing of all.</blockquote><br /></span>

<div id="review_110956109" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/110956109" />
    <a title="Emily" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/343944-emily"><img alt="Emily" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1242156693p2/343944.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/110956109?book_show_action=true">Jul 10, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily" href="/user/show/343944-emily">Emily</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/343944-emily?shelf=second-childhood">second-childhood</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer110956109" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2626163363135474636">Depending on your point of view, I have either read this book twice (once twenty years ago, and once last week), or I've read two different books one time each. Moominpappa's Memoirs is a revised edition of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/222605.The_Exploits_of_Moominpappa__Puffin_Books_' title='The Exploits of Moominpappa (Puffin Books) by Tove Jansson' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Exploits of Moominpappa</a>. It seems Jansson went back and rewrote and added bits to the original not long after its first English translation was published. The English language publishers apparently chose to pretend this hadn't happened (it must indeed have been quite vexing for them) and </span>
  <span id="freeText2626163363135474636" style="display:none">Depending on your point of view, I have either read this book twice (once twenty years ago, and once last week), or I've read two different books one time each. Moominpappa's Memoirs is a revised edition of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/222605.The_Exploits_of_Moominpappa__Puffin_Books_" title="The Exploits of Moominpappa (Puffin Books) by Tove Jansson" rel="nofollow noopener">The Exploits of Moominpappa</a>. It seems Jansson went back and rewrote and added bits to the original not long after its first English translation was published. The English language publishers apparently chose to pretend this hadn't happened (it must indeed have been quite vexing for them) and kept reprinting the original. A new translation was finally published in 1994.<br /><br />So the burning question is: did I feel completely baffled by the unfamiliarity of much of this book because time had warped my memory, or because Jansson changed it so much? I had remembered it as a light-hearted romp much in the vein of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/79549.Finn_Family_Moomintroll__Moomintrolls_" title="Finn Family Moomintroll (Moomintrolls) by Tove Jansson" rel="nofollow noopener">Finn Family Moomintroll</a> with lots of gentle absurdity and a fast-paced story, so I was eager to read it to my son, who I'm quite sure is not ready for the more disquieting tone of the later books. But upon setting forth on the story with my eager boy by my side, I saw at once that as a read aloud it would not suit. Jansson pokes fun at Moominpappa's pretentiousness and self-importance by having him narrate the story of his youth in the most ridiculously overblown pompous way, making a melodrama of everything (yet you can tell she's fond of him despite this). Here's a fairly typical passage from the first chapter:<br /><br /><i>...by and by a change came: I started to muse about the shape of my nose. I put my trivial surroundings aside and mused more and more about myself, and I found this to be a bewitching occupation. I stopped asking and longed instead to speak of my thoughts and feelings. Alas, there was no one besides myself who found me interesting.</i><br /><br />I felt that this, and some even more abstract passages, was asking a bit too much of my son. Moomintroll, who, along with Sniff and Snuffkin is hearing the memoirs read aloud, sums it up pretty well:<br /><br /><i>"Pappa," said Moomintroll, "did one really talk in that unnatural way in those days?"</i><br /><br />I quickly decided that I would enjoy this book much more reading it to myself, and for a few nights "forgot" to continue where we'd left off (harsh, I know).<br /><br />On picking it up for myself, I found that ironically, after that highly ponderous first chapter, the fast-paced story I remembered got started. There are some funny bits. I like the boat, which was supposed to be christened "The Ocean Orchestra", but after being painted by an inept speller, is referred to as "The Oshun Oxtra" for the duration. Edward the Booble, an gigantic creature who constantly has to pay for the funerals of the creatures he steps on was mildly amusing, in a slap-sticky kind of way. There is a somewhat deeper thread to the book, in the conflict between Moominpappa's longing for adventure and his charming instinct to build houses with fretwork in a pine-cone motif. The most surprising parts of the book, both twenty years ago and now, were the revelations about Sniff and Snuffkin's respective parentage. The denoument of this felt rushed and puzzling though-- not to be spoilerish, but where had all these suddenly appearing characters been all this time? And where did they all disappear to afterwords? It was incidentally, satisfying (to a degree) to be reading the series for the first time ever in publication order, and to understand where the Mymble's Daughter and Little My came from, those two being firmly ensconced, with no explanation given, in the Moomin household at the start of the next book.<br /><br />This is a strange entry in the series, but not unrewarding.<br /><br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="2626163363135474636" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1147837081" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1147837081" />
    <a title="Drew" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5719060-drew"><img alt="Drew" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1492889428p2/5719060.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1147837081?book_show_action=true">Dec 30, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Drew" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Drew" href="/user/show/5719060-drew">Drew</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780312625436" href="/book/show/8258821-moominpappa-s-memoirs">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5719060-drew?shelf=read_to_kids">read_to_kids</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1147837081" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3442595172055670590">Of the three Moomin books I've read so far, this one is the deepest and most philosophical. That probably makes it the most "adult" of these alleged children's books. <br/><br/>Of course, they've all got traces of wisdom and philosophy in them, but it really emerges here, where Moominpappa sets out to write his life story. Like the other books, it's warmly absurd and imbued with deep emotion. Moominpappa considers himself quite special, born under important stars, resulting in an expressed desire for adve</span>
  <span id="freeText3442595172055670590" style="display:none">Of the three Moomin books I've read so far, this one is the deepest and most philosophical. That probably makes it the most "adult" of these alleged children's books. <br /><br />Of course, they've all got traces of wisdom and philosophy in them, but it really emerges here, where Moominpappa sets out to write his life story. Like the other books, it's warmly absurd and imbued with deep emotion. Moominpappa considers himself quite special, born under important stars, resulting in an expressed desire for adventure. He finds adventure on a riverboat, along with characters who are eventually revealed to be Snufkin's and Sniff's fathers. <br /><br />But even on his adventures, there is still an undercurrent of longing and yearning. Near the end of the book, as his fellow adventurers begin to settle down into careers and get married (or otherwise paired off) Moominpappa despairs that his life of adventure is probably over. Raise your hand if you can relate to that! <i> :: raises hand :: </i><br /><br />Ironically, as more and more people fill his house, the more lonely and isolated he feels. Classic introvert. In fact, I think Jansson captures the introvert personality quite well in all her books. (Snufkin's need to frequently withdraw from people is one clear example.) <br /><br />Moominpappa is me. I am Moominpappa. <br /><br />Never fear. The story ends on a high note as new adventures come washing in with the tide. Literally. <br /><br />I can't speak highly enough of this series. Through her whimsical cast of non-human characters, Jansson has captured the human experience, in stories that have you nodding along and saying "Yes, life is just like that." <br /><br />If this hadn't been a library book, I would have been highlighting passages on nearly every page. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3442595172055670590" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_226756120" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/226756120" />
    <a title="Sean D&#39;angelo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/546909-sean-d-angelo"><img alt="Sean D&#39;angelo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1319417697p2/546909.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/226756120?book_show_action=true">Oct 23, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sean D&#39;angelo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sean D&#39;angelo" href="/user/show/546909-sean-d-angelo">Sean D&#39;angelo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer226756120" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8129011239706556292">As far as Tove Jansson's work goes, Moominpappa's Memoirs may be better suited for the more mature and philosophical children (or nostalgic adults like myself). It's definitely not a bedtime read. But in my opinion no other book in the Moomin series captures quite so well the pure whimsical delight of Jansson's imagination. In fact, it's the only one that's ever brought a tear of joy to my eye.<br/><br/>For those who have read and enjoyed other Moomintroll books, don't be discouraged by the absence of you</span>
  <span id="freeText8129011239706556292" style="display:none">As far as Tove Jansson's work goes, Moominpappa's Memoirs may be better suited for the more mature and philosophical children (or nostalgic adults like myself). It's definitely not a bedtime read. But in my opinion no other book in the Moomin series captures quite so well the pure whimsical delight of Jansson's imagination. In fact, it's the only one that's ever brought a tear of joy to my eye.<br /><br />For those who have read and enjoyed other Moomintroll books, don't be discouraged by the absence of your favorite little critters — Moominpappa and his friends are cut from the same cloth as his young wards Moomintroll, Sniff, and Snufkin. Their trials are every bit as fraught with excitement, mystery, and wonder. Their dreams are just as far fetched. And while Moominpappa is always one to linger on internal monologue, these introspective moments come off as silly rather than cumbersome.<br /><br />For those who haven't yet had the pleasure of entering Tove Jansson's fantastical world, my advice is pick up another of the books first — I highly recommend starting with Finn Family Moomintroll — and then return to Moominpappa's Memoirs down the road. If you are anything like me, you won't be able to help yourself.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8129011239706556292" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer546394265" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer17584987942356639992">This is one of my all time favourite books. This is the edition I read as a child whilst swinging in a hammock on summer holidays at our farm. It was the first Moomin book I had read, although it is not the first in the sequence. I'm so grateful to have been introduced to the work of the stellar Tove Jansson as a child, because her work for children and adults has given me immense pleasure over the years. <br/><br/>She was outstanding as an artist as well as a writer. Most of all she inspires me still wit</span>
  <span id="freeText17584987942356639992" style="display:none">This is one of my all time favourite books. This is the edition I read as a child whilst swinging in a hammock on summer holidays at our farm. It was the first Moomin book I had read, although it is not the first in the sequence. I'm so grateful to have been introduced to the work of the stellar Tove Jansson as a child, because her work for children and adults has given me immense pleasure over the years. <br /><br />She was outstanding as an artist as well as a writer. Most of all she inspires me still with the wisdom and perceptiveness she shows through her quirky characters and their experiences of life, politics, culture, nature and relationships. The underlying message in all of the work I have read by Jansson is to live life to the full and love it, despite its complexity, irrationality, troublesomeness and scary bits! <br /><br />Oh, and family and hospitality are strong themes too. The impression I get, is that if I'd turned up on Jansson's doorstep one evening, with no luggage and wearing nothing but a ragged fancy dress costume and carrying a dead mouse, she would have welcomed me in and made a bed for me on the sofa, and probably pancakes the next morning (at whatever time I arose.) She would also have helped with a suitable funeral for the mouse: flower garlands, morning tea and possibly a poem. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17584987942356639992" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText5182523830400308591" style="display:none">Interesting to contrast this with later books in the series like <i>November</i> or <i>Moominpappa at Sea</i> -- this is a much more joyful and zany book, and while it's one of the few Moomin stories that feels directly satirical, it's also one of the most child friendly. I found reading this very comforting, although it isn't as emotionally resonant as some of the other books. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8030380276527443529">For whatever reason, we struggled early to connect with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/224538.Moominpappa_s_Memoirs__The_Moomins___4_' title='Moominpappa's Memoirs (The Moomins, #4) by Tove Jansson' rel='nofollow noopener'>Moominpappa's Memoirs</a>. Moominpappa depicts himself from page 1 as a somewhat unlikeable egotist. Not surprisingly, Jansson’s gentle sense of humor transforms everything, and Moominpappa becomes adorable in the end:<blockquote>“Let me stop here, at this remarkable turning point of my stormy youth, let me close my Memoirs at the moment when the most wonderful of Moomins comes into my life! Since then my follies have been supervised by her gentle and unde</blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText8030380276527443529" style="display:none">For whatever reason, we struggled early to connect with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/224538.Moominpappa_s_Memoirs__The_Moomins___4_" title="Moominpappa's Memoirs (The Moomins, #4) by Tove Jansson" rel="nofollow noopener">Moominpappa's Memoirs</a>. Moominpappa depicts himself from page 1 as a somewhat unlikeable egotist. Not surprisingly, Jansson’s gentle sense of humor transforms everything, and Moominpappa becomes adorable in the end:<blockquote>“Let me stop here, at this remarkable turning point of my stormy youth, let me close my Memoirs at the moment when the most wonderful of Moomins comes into my life! Since then my follies have been supervised by her gentle and understanding eyes, and thereby transformed into sense and wisdom while, however, losing none of the enchantment and love of freedom that have led me to write them down.”</blockquote>Awwww! We’re smitten by the relationship between the Moomin parents.<br /><br />Hats off to Jansson for her illustration of underwater action on page 134. It’s beautiful, rivaling her amazing artwork throughout <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1003725.Comet_in_Moominland__The_Moomins___2_" title="Comet in Moominland (The Moomins, #2) by Tove Jansson" rel="nofollow noopener">Comet in Moominland</a>.<br /><br />If the opinions of others are to be believed, the best’s yet to come in an already solid series. Can’t wait!</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1574555307" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13326038887420072700">Yet another fun one! I loved getting to read Moominpappa's memoirs -- such escapades, such oddness, such fun! :) Moominpappa has quite a "feel" to his storytelling. It's great. Also the Joxter was fun -- nice to know where Snufkin's slightly lawless ways originated. ;) So much fun! And I especially loved how the memoirs would pause occasionally as Moominpappa is interrupted in his reading by Moomintroll, Sniff, and Snufkin, as they ask questions about the story and their various daddies' adventu</span>
  <span id="freeText13326038887420072700" style="display:none">Yet another fun one! I loved getting to read Moominpappa's memoirs -- such escapades, such oddness, such fun! :) Moominpappa has quite a "feel" to his storytelling. It's great. Also the Joxter was fun -- nice to know where Snufkin's slightly lawless ways originated. ;) So much fun! And I especially loved how the memoirs would pause occasionally as Moominpappa is interrupted in his reading by Moomintroll, Sniff, and Snufkin, as they ask questions about the story and their various daddies' adventures. Loved that! And the way that it all came together at the end was marvelous. :D The Moomin books are just loads of bizarre whimsical fun. On to the next one!</span>
  <a data-text-id="13326038887420072700" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Perhaps it was just because the narrative style is different than the others, but there's other things: for example, one chapter ends like this: <br/><br/>"'Nibling,' I said to end this surprising conversation, 'what'll your mother say when she finds that you've run away?'<br/><br/>'She'll cry, I believe,' said the Nibling." <br/><br/>And that's it.   <span id="freeText11810196062669972522" style="display:none">The Moomin books are all quite odd, but this was the oddest so far. That's the end of the chapter. It's so surreal, sometimes I felt like I was reading it in a dream. That being said, I really enjoyed this book and the ghost is now one of my top favourite characters in literature. </span>

<div id="review_3734078" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3734078" />
    <a title="Suvi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/59357-suvi"><img alt="Suvi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1537657400p2/59357.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3734078?book_show_action=true">Jul 29, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Suvi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Suvi" href="/user/show/59357-suvi">Suvi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780374350451" href="/book/show/545138.Moominpappa_s_Memoirs">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59357-suvi?shelf=children">children</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59357-suvi?shelf=1940-1969">1940-1969</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59357-suvi?shelf=_book-shelf">_book-shelf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59357-suvi?shelf=_europe-northern">_europe-northern</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3734078" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1218067384365376758">Here Moominpappa gets the chance to tell with his own words about his younger years. A dismal childhood in an orphanage and the feeling of not being loved or appreciated changes into great adventures with Hodgkins and his ship. Moominpappa's narrative voice is pompous and self-centered but not the least bit annoying. The satirizing of the memoir genre gives a special air to the whole book.<br/><br/>Several of my favourite scenes from the tv-series are included: a female Hemulen gets rescued from Groke and</span>
  <span id="freeText1218067384365376758" style="display:none">Here Moominpappa gets the chance to tell with his own words about his younger years. A dismal childhood in an orphanage and the feeling of not being loved or appreciated changes into great adventures with Hodgkins and his ship. Moominpappa's narrative voice is pompous and self-centered but not the least bit annoying. The satirizing of the memoir genre gives a special air to the whole book.<br /><br />Several of my favourite scenes from the tv-series are included: a female Hemulen gets rescued from Groke and tries to push her educational values on the ship's bohemian coffee-drinking crew, the deep sea dive with all the mysterious fish with lamps, and the slightly inept Island Ghost.<br /><br />Two characters have been more hazy to me until now. Joxter is very similar to Snufkin, only a bit more lazy. Snufkin seems to have inherited all his good qualities: criticism towards excessive rules, drifting, and enjoying life. Mymble is busy popping out new kids every once in a while and seems to be very liberal in her parenting (reading scary stories to her brood at night and merely laughing at their shenanigans), not to mention the affair with Joxter. Good for you, Mymble, although I'm not sure Joxter is a very suitable father.<br /><br />There's of course the one thread throughout which gives this a more serious undertone. After gaining his independence Moominpappa constantly struggles between the need of having his own family and the need for adventure. There's a beautiful and poignant passage at the end where Moominpappa muses that friends are starting families or gaining a new position in the world. They begin to be scared of the rain while he is becoming increasingly lonely.<br /><br />Although it becomes evident later on that despite of settling down Moominpappa never abandons the possibility to go on an adventure, and learns to balance his needs with domesticity, the conflict between the two opposite desires (along with the feeling of disappointment of never achieving enough) takes the book into darker waters and paves the road to later themes.<br /><br /><i>"I cannot stress enough the perils of your friends marrying or becoming court inventors. One day you are all a society of outlaws, adventurous comrades and companions who will be pushing off somewhere or other when things become tiresome; you have all the world to choose from, just by looking at the map… And then, suddenly, they’re not interested any more. They want to keep warm. They’re afraid of rain. They start collecting big things that can’t fit in a rucksack. They talk only of small things. They don’t like to make sudden decisions and do something contrariwise. Formerly they hoisted sail; now they carpenter little shelves for porcelain mugs."</i><br /><br /><i>"'Well,' said Hodgkins, 'perhaps he really is interested in everything, only he doesn't overdo it. For ourselves there is always one single interest. You want to become. I want to do. My nephew wants to have. But the Joxter just lives.'<br /><br />'Simply lives,' I said. 'Anybody can do that.'<br /><br />'Mphm,' Hodgkins said."</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="1218067384365376758" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_515197925" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/515197925" />
    <a title="Graychin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1013182-graychin"><img alt="Graychin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597960333p2/1013182.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/515197925?book_show_action=true">Jan 23, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Graychin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Graychin" href="/user/show/1013182-graychin">Graychin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer515197925" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12702843828577956692">I was sick at home with the flu recently when my daughter told me I should read this book. It begins with Moominpappa in bed with a cold, acting like a baby, afraid he’s going to die and that all the treasure of his life experiences will be forever uncommemorated. So he sits up and begins writing his memoirs. He has very romantic notions about himself. He was born, he says, under propitious stars. Though an orphan, he suspects he is a child of royalty. His life, from its earliest days, was one m</span>
  <span id="freeText12702843828577956692" style="display:none">I was sick at home with the flu recently when my daughter told me I should read this book. It begins with Moominpappa in bed with a cold, acting like a baby, afraid he’s going to die and that all the treasure of his life experiences will be forever uncommemorated. So he sits up and begins writing his memoirs. He has very romantic notions about himself. He was born, he says, under propitious stars. Though an orphan, he suspects he is a child of royalty. His life, from its earliest days, was one marked for adventure. And what an adventure his youth was! - at least according to his only slightly embellished recounting of it.<br /><br />I wish I’d read these books when I was my daughter’s age. I’m glad that my children love them so much. They’re wonderfully politically incorrect. Rum toddies are consumed two or three times, for example. We’re also informed, by no less an authority than Moominmamma, that pipe smoking can’t be unhealthy because nothing really pleasant can be bad for you. Am I a bad father for smiling at this? Don’t be ridiculous. I am the World’s Best Papa and have the hand-drawn and colored card on my desk to prove it. I just maybe need to quit acting like such a big baby when I stay home sick.<br /><br />Finally, I’ll offer the following thought from Moominpappa himself, on the sometimes melancholy changes that come with adulthood:<br /><br /><i>“I cannot stress enough the perils of your friends marrying or becoming court inventors. One day you are all a society of outlaws, adventurous comrades and companions who will be pushing off somewhere or other when things become tiresome; you have all the world to choose from, just by looking at the map… And then, suddenly, they’re not interested any more. They want to keep warm. They’re afraid of rain. They start collecting big things that can’t fit in a rucksack. They talk only of small things. They don’t like to make sudden decisions and do something contrariwise. Formerly they hoisted sail; now they carpenter little shelves for porcelain mugs.”</i><br /><br />I do like a nice mug these days.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12702843828577956692" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1294891214" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1294891214" />
    <a title="Jennifer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/83139-jennifer"><img alt="Jennifer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1505315164p2/83139.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1294891214?book_show_action=true">May 31, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jennifer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jennifer" href="/user/show/83139-jennifer">Jennifer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780312625436" href="/book/show/8258821-moominpappa-s-memoirs">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83139-jennifer?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83139-jennifer?shelf=owned">owned</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1294891214" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6712727008601264245">So, I am always checking out the middle grades fiction section at my local bookstore, looking for books for Jefferson as well as books for my We Need Diverse Books challenge supporting his classroom. The day I was scouring the shelves and found a set of <i>all</i> of Jansson's Moomin novels, I may have done a little happy dance. I definitely made a strange animal noise of some kind.<br/><br/>At some point in my childhood, I was gifted with a copy of <i>Tales from Moominvalley</i> by my Uncle Tom, and I quickly realized</span>
  <span id="freeText6712727008601264245" style="display:none">So, I am always checking out the middle grades fiction section at my local bookstore, looking for books for Jefferson as well as books for my We Need Diverse Books challenge supporting his classroom. The day I was scouring the shelves and found a set of <i>all</i> of Jansson's Moomin novels, I may have done a little happy dance. I definitely made a strange animal noise of some kind.<br /><br />At some point in my childhood, I was gifted with a copy of <i>Tales from Moominvalley</i> by my Uncle Tom, and I quickly realized it was one of the best books ever. It took me a much longer time to realize that it wasn't the only Moomin book out there, and I can't tell you how many times I've looked for Jansson on the shelves of various bookstores, only to slowly accumulate three or four more of the series, over decades.<br /><br />Now that I was staring at brightly colored versions of all eight, I couldn't let this chance pass me by, despite the fact that I sadly have still not catalogued by entire book collection, and couldn't remember exactly which ones I was still missing. (I did end up having to exchange one of the new ones I bought.)<br /><br />One of the new books went into my surprise box for reading out loud on a road trip, but this one skipped to the front of my to-read list. I had some concerns, as Moominpappa has never been my favorite character, and most of the other characters are largely absent. But this turned out to be quite lovely, about not knowing where one fits in, and being torn between the desire to have grand adventures and the desire to build a cozy, ornately decorated home. Large parts of the story are absurd, of course, but mostly in a charming way. And finally getting an origin story for Mymble's Daughter and Little My (among others, but you know it's Little My I really care about) was quite satisfying.<br /><br />Does not quite make it to the level of <i>Moominland Midwinter</i> or <i>Tales from Moominvalley</i>, but those two are, in my opinion, quite near perfection.<br /><br />Now I want to go read <i>Moominland Midwinter</i> again.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6712727008601264245" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_766089066" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/766089066" />
    <a title="Karl Orbell" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7334020-karl-orbell"><img alt="Karl Orbell" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1325723494p2/7334020.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/766089066?book_show_action=true">Nov 15, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Karl Orbell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Karl Orbell" href="/user/show/7334020-karl-orbell">Karl Orbell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780140303230" href="/book/show/222605.The_Exploits_of_Moominpappa_Described_by_Himself">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer766089066" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14090613563763014324">Two things I have learnt from this book.<br/><br/><blockquote>
<br/>1. Moominpappa is a narcissistic pillock.<br/>2. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/45230.Tove_Jansson' title='Tove Jansson' rel='nofollow noopener'>Tove Jansson</a> can't write in the first person at all well.<br/>
</blockquote><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1409243663ra/10953300.gif' width='245' height='188' alt='Moominpappa lifting weights' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Nevertheless, this little novel is presented as the memoirs of Moominpappa, and serves as a history for the other Moomin books, so it's a necessary read within the series.<br/><br/>We are introduced to the fathers of Snufkin and Sniff, and eventually their mothers too, not all quite alike their children, but sufficiently so to imagine that this is just any other st</span>
  <span id="freeText14090613563763014324" style="display:none">Two things I have learnt from this book.<br><br><blockquote>
<br>1. Moominpappa is a narcissistic pillock.<br>2. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/45230.Tove_Jansson" title="Tove Jansson" rel="nofollow noopener">Tove Jansson</a> can't write in the first person at all well.<br>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1409243663ra/10953300.gif" width="245" height="188" alt="Moominpappa lifting weights" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Nevertheless, this little novel is presented as the memoirs of Moominpappa, and serves as a history for the other Moomin books, so it's a necessary read within the series.<br><br>We are introduced to the fathers of Snufkin and Sniff, and eventually their mothers too, not all quite alike their children, but sufficiently so to imagine that this is just any other story with the parents in the usual protagonists roles. Like a flashback in a comedy where the cast get a stupid haircut and old clothing and that's that.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1409243663i/10953301._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="265" alt="Moominpappa and the gang" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>For the first time, Little My turns up, albeit via her mother and big sister for the majority of the time, though her first few words are towards the end - not that she has joined the gang yet.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1409243663i/10953302.jpg" width="252" height="400" alt="Little My" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Otherwise it is the usual Moomin stock, high adventure upon the seas and land, the building of cunning modes of transport and habitation and a certain disregard for logic or common sense.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1409243663i/10953303._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="286" alt="Moominpappa and the Ghost" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>At least there's an engineer in this one, who likes cogs. I do wish the female characters were more than hat stands though.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14090613563763014324" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">fans of the Moomins</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40593416-lobsterquadrille?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40593416-lobsterquadrille?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40593416-lobsterquadrille?shelf=children-s-literature">children-s-literature</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40593416-lobsterquadrille?shelf=funny">funny</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1758267963" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10825952450461578263">3.5 stars<br/><br/> <i>Moominpappa's Memoirs</i> is really a story within a story, in which Moominpappa is telling the story of his adventurous youth to Moomintroll, Sniff, and Snufkin. During Moominpappa's travels, he meets the eccentric characters who would become the parents of Sniff and Snufkin, as well as his own future wife. <br/> <i>Moominpappa's Memoirs</i> is of course quite funny and creative at times, introducing some fun new characters. The ghost, Edward the Booble, and the bossy Hemulen Aunts are entertaining, </span>
  <span id="freeText10825952450461578263" style="display:none">3.5 stars<br /><br /> <i>Moominpappa's Memoirs</i> is really a story within a story, in which Moominpappa is telling the story of his adventurous youth to Moomintroll, Sniff, and Snufkin. During Moominpappa's travels, he meets the eccentric characters who would become the parents of Sniff and Snufkin, as well as his own future wife. <br /> <i>Moominpappa's Memoirs</i> is of course quite funny and creative at times, introducing some fun new characters. The ghost, Edward the Booble, and the bossy Hemulen Aunts are entertaining, despite not showing up in the story a great deal. The Mymbles can be pretty amusing too, though I would have liked to see more of Little My in the story. <br /> The ending was nice, but it didn't make much sense. The parents of Snufkin and Sniff are all apparently alive and well, so why on earth haven't they raised them themselves? How did Snufkin end up wandering the world rather than being raised with his countless half-siblings? Why does Sniff just live with the Moomins instead of with his own parents? I may be over-analyzing, but I just can't help wondering about this. <br /><br /> This was a pleasant light read, but I didn't like it as much as I liked <i>Finn Family Moomintroll</i>.<br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="10825952450461578263" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer543389167249834286">As Moominpappa writes his memoirs, he describes the adventures he and creatures he encountered as young Moomin. He describes how he ran away from home, travelled the world and how he eventually met Moominmamma. <br/><br/>I thoroughly enjoyed reading this book and I consider it to be timeless. Jansson’s imagination and ability to be highly descriptive but brief really makes the story move quickly and holds the reader’s attention. The book jumps effortlessly between the present and the past. I think that Ja</span>
  <span id="freeText543389167249834286" style="display:none">As Moominpappa writes his memoirs, he describes the adventures he and creatures he encountered as young Moomin. He describes how he ran away from home, travelled the world and how he eventually met Moominmamma. <br /><br />I thoroughly enjoyed reading this book and I consider it to be timeless. Jansson’s imagination and ability to be highly descriptive but brief really makes the story move quickly and holds the reader’s attention. The book jumps effortlessly between the present and the past. I think that Janssons style of writing could really help inspire children of all ages and this book in particular is an excellent example of how imaginative writing should be done. Some of the vocabulary in the book might be a little confusing for some children. This might be due to the translation between languages but, the majority of the text is highly accessible to children. A book that I would definitely choose for carpet/circle time.<br /></span>

Moominpappa is embarrassingly convinced of his self-importance but is still a lovable character. Hodgkins, the Muddler and Joxter are all as different from each other as they are from Moominpappa and this creates a wonderful cast of characters. Moominpappa is very ambitious and wants to become a famous adventurer. He does not understand the Joxter who is happy just being. This conversation between Moominpappa an</span>
  <span id="freeText3250019682500199201" style="display:none">In this installment of the Moomin series we follow the story of Moominpappa's youth. Moominpappa is embarrassingly convinced of his self-importance but is still a lovable character. Hodgkins, the Muddler and Joxter are all as different from each other as they are from Moominpappa and this creates a wonderful cast of characters. Moominpappa is very ambitious and wants to become a famous adventurer. He does not understand the Joxter who is happy just being. This conversation between Moominpappa and Hodgkins illustrates the different attitudes to life:<br /><br /><blockquote>"Well," said Hodgkins, "perhaps he really is interested in everything, only he doesn't overdo it. For ourselves there is always one single interest. You want to become. I want to do. My nephew wants to have. But the Joxter just lives."<br /><br />"Simply lives," I said. "Anybody can do that."<br /><br />"Mphm," Hodgkins said.</blockquote><br /><br />Perhaps simply living is the most difficult of all...?</span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer135623755" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9767290539213867321">I admit to being a little disappointed when I discovered that this was not the story of Moominpappa's adventures following the Hattifatteners, but I soon came round to embrace this strange tale of fathers: Moomintroll's, Sniff's, and Snufkin's, respectively. I was a little concerned that Sniff and Snufkin appeared to have never even met their parents, but I guess in Moominland that's not such a crazy notion. Anyway, this is Moominpappa's somewhat embellished account of his early years, from his </span>
  <span id="freeText9767290539213867321" style="display:none">I admit to being a little disappointed when I discovered that this was not the story of Moominpappa's adventures following the Hattifatteners, but I soon came round to embrace this strange tale of fathers: Moomintroll's, Sniff's, and Snufkin's, respectively. I was a little concerned that Sniff and Snufkin appeared to have never even met their parents, but I guess in Moominland that's not such a crazy notion. Anyway, this is Moominpappa's somewhat embellished account of his early years, from his abandonment at a Hemulen-run orphanage to the day he met Moominmamma. I was truly entertained by the Autocrat's speeches, and the art was wonderful as always, but this was not my favorite Moomin book. Moominpappa's inflated sense of self-importance was amusing at first, but became tiresome by the end. Luckily, it's a very short book, and does not overstay its welcome.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9767290539213867321" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2243965459" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6803506934889619559">The Memoirs of Moominpappa is again wonderfully illustrated and a lovely book to add to my hardback collection!<br/><br/>This book focuses on Moominpappa himself and his life and while this is still an enjoyable read, I found I missed the involvement of the other characters like Moominmamma, Moomintroll, Snork and the Snork-Maiden. For this book a number of other characters were introduced but perhaps too many new faces was introduced at once! <br/><br/>The book centres around Moominpappas journey at sea, and I fou</span>
  <span id="freeText6803506934889619559" style="display:none">The Memoirs of Moominpappa is again wonderfully illustrated and a lovely book to add to my hardback collection!<br /><br />This book focuses on Moominpappa himself and his life and while this is still an enjoyable read, I found I missed the involvement of the other characters like Moominmamma, Moomintroll, Snork and the Snork-Maiden. For this book a number of other characters were introduced but perhaps too many new faces was introduced at once! <br /><br />The book centres around Moominpappas journey at sea, and I found this section to be a lot longer than necessary! I particularly enjoyed the beginning, where you find out Moominpappas birth and his exciting exit from the foundling home to start his adventuring and the ending where he meets Moominmamma! Whilst still a good Moomin read, I felt the middle section could have been more exciting and the writing style was different from the last two!<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6803506934889619559" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer7935914018941485757">Continuing on with my mission to re read all the Moomin books this year.<br/><br/>This is the tale of Moominpappa's youth - growing up at a Hemulen-run orphanage for young Moomins, and setting out on his first adventures, all narrated by Moominpappa in his very modest way. You get to find out where Little My (one of my favourite characters) comes from - an island ruled by a King who doesn't want anyone to feel inferior or in awe to him so insists they call him Daddy Jones. Little My is in the story, but I</span>
  <span id="freeText7935914018941485757" style="display:none">Continuing on with my mission to re read all the Moomin books this year.<br /><br />This is the tale of Moominpappa's youth - growing up at a Hemulen-run orphanage for young Moomins, and setting out on his first adventures, all narrated by Moominpappa in his very modest way. You get to find out where Little My (one of my favourite characters) comes from - an island ruled by a King who doesn't want anyone to feel inferior or in awe to him so insists they call him Daddy Jones. Little My is in the story, but I think in this one for pure eccentricity and general awkwardness she is completely upstaged by Edward the Booble.<br /><br />The imagination in these books is fantastic, and as always there are great illustrations. <br /><br />2016 note - review from my 2007 bookcrossing journal.</span>

<div id="review_188328768" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/188328768" />
    <a title="James Perkins" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5862728-james-perkins"><img alt="James Perkins" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1321259579p2/5862728.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/188328768?book_show_action=true">Jul 24, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="James Perkins" class="user" itemprop="url" name="James Perkins" href="/user/show/5862728-james-perkins">James Perkins</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer188328768" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7588628092128982476">Another bizarre but hugely entertaining volume about the cute Finnish traditional children's icons, the Moomins. This one tells the story of how Moominpappa encountered a series of weird beings who then became the parents of his friends in Moomin Valley. It also chronicles his first meeting with Moominmamma, his wife - although how the naked, hippopotamus-like creatures produced their son Moomintroll without the aid of any genitalia is anyone's guess. With her surreal imagery and odd wit, Tove J</span>
  <span id="freeText7588628092128982476" style="display:none">Another bizarre but hugely entertaining volume about the cute Finnish traditional children's icons, the Moomins. This one tells the story of how Moominpappa encountered a series of weird beings who then became the parents of his friends in Moomin Valley. It also chronicles his first meeting with Moominmamma, his wife - although how the naked, hippopotamus-like creatures produced their son Moomintroll without the aid of any genitalia is anyone's guess. With her surreal imagery and odd wit, Tove Jansson has offered a unique insight into the Finnish way of thinking as the stories caricature the Finnish character, as well as provide a series of very amusing tales for both adults and children alike. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7588628092128982476" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1259853895" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1259853895" />
    <a title="Stephen Curran" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11677504-stephen-curran"><img alt="Stephen Curran" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1574349718p2/11677504.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1259853895?book_show_action=true">Apr 20, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stephen Curran" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stephen Curran" href="/user/show/11677504-stephen-curran">Stephen Curran</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1259853895" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7995175448518705906">Over the first three Moomins books, Moominpappa can been seen quietly working away at his memoirs. Here, we finally get to read the fruits of his labour.<br/><br/>The youthful adventures he recounts are great fun, enhanced by the usual vivid descriptions of nature. The reactions of Sniff and Snufkin as they hear about their parents for the first time are sweetly moving and the ending is downright romantic. "Life is short," says Moominpappa, "the world is enormous."<br/><br/>The illustrations are as beautiful as eve</span>
  <span id="freeText7995175448518705906" style="display:none">Over the first three Moomins books, Moominpappa can been seen quietly working away at his memoirs. Here, we finally get to read the fruits of his labour.<br /><br />The youthful adventures he recounts are great fun, enhanced by the usual vivid descriptions of nature. The reactions of Sniff and Snufkin as they hear about their parents for the first time are sweetly moving and the ending is downright romantic. "Life is short," says Moominpappa, "the world is enormous."<br /><br />The illustrations are as beautiful as ever; my favourite in the series so far. In fact, I have framed prints of two of them hanging on my living room wall: the Garden of Surprises, and the submerged amphibian Oshun Oxtra surrounded by the creatures of the sea.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7995175448518705906" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('IjvGXcf/yxyYYHBJXPvq7NF9pYpV4K7Y5/YuVavxTLB0JrOH/FRGe4WW4PdcteXZwXSFVhiJmZxwDdG/Vnpa5g==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/45230.Tove_Jansson">About Tove Jansson</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer10612859538858554278"><b>Tove Jansson</b> was born and died in Helsinki, Finland. As a Finnish citizen whose mother tongue was Swedish, she was part of the Swedish-speaking Finns minority. Thus, all her books were originally written in Swedish.<br/><br/>Although known first and foremost as an author, Tove Jansson considered her careers as author and painter to be of equal importance. <br/><br/>Tove Jansson wrote and illustrated her first <i>Moomin</i> </span>
  <span id="freeText10612859538858554278" style="display:none"><b>Tove Jansson</b> was born and died in Helsinki, Finland. As a Finnish citizen whose mother tongue was Swedish, she was part of the Swedish-speaking Finns minority. Thus, all her books were originally written in Swedish.<br /><br />Although known first and foremost as an author, Tove Jansson considered her careers as author and painter to be of equal importance. <br /><br />Tove Jansson wrote and illustrated her first <i>Moomin</i> book, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3300083-the-moomins-and-the-great-flood" rel="nofollow noopener">The Moomins and the Great Flood</a> (1945), during World War II. She said later that the war had depressed her, and she had wanted to write something naive and innocent. Besides the <i>Moomin</i> novels and short stories, Tove Jansson also wrote and illustrated four original and highly popular picture books.<br /><br />Jansson's <i>Moomin</i> books have been translated into 33 languages. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10612859538858554278" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

In the United States the series beginning with Finn Family Moomintroll (first published in English in 1945) has accumulated generations of fans. Since Farrar, Straus and Giroux began reissuing the books in 1989, grateful readers old and new have been thrilled to have the stories available again. At last the final installment is being published – oddly, the only book that features none of the Moomin family themselves, though it does take place at their house. There familiar characters converge – Snufkin, the Hemulen, Fillyjonk, and others – seeking out the Moomins\' welcoming company, only to find them absent. All remain at the house, all have very different personalities that clash often, but something about their homey cohabitation during the icy winter changes each visitor in a gratifying way.
